Abidjan, the largest city in Ivory Coast, is a significant urban center with a total area of 2,119 square kilometers and a population of 6,321,017. Located at an elevation of 18 meters, it serves as the capital of the Lagunes Region and the Sud Department. The city is known for its motto, "District d'Abidjan, acteur de développement," reflecting its role in national development. Abidjan is situated in the GMT time zone and has the telephone area code +225. As the economic and political hub of Ivory Coast, Abidjan hosts the Parliament of Ivory Coast and is the headquarters for various organizations such as the Democratic Party of Ivory Coast – African Democratic Rally, Incubateur Régional d'Afrique de l'Ouest, and Interivoire. The city is also home to the Ivorian Republican Guard and serves as the garrison location for this military unit. Culturally, Abidjan boasts landmarks like the Culture Palace of Abidjan and Village Ivoire, which are central to the city's cultural scene. It has been the venue for major events, including the 2009 African Nations Championship Final and the 1984 African Cup of Nations Final. The University of Science and Technology of Ivory Coast is also located here, contributing to the region's educational landscape. Sports enthusiasts in Abidjan support teams such as JC d'Abidjan, Stade d'Abidjan, and Stella Club d'Adjamé, which are based in the city. Abidjan's influence extends to the music industry, being the hometown of notable artists like Magic System and Ak47 (rapper). Universal Music Africa also has a presence in the city, further highlighting its cultural significance. Abidjan is the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Priscille Kreto, Robert Sankara, and Roger Aholou. It is also where figures like Robert Guéï, Christian Bonaud, and Christian Lattier passed away. The city's diverse population, known as Abidjanais, contributes to its vibrant atmosphere, making it a focal point of activity in Ivory Coast.
Addis Ababa, the capital of Ethiopia, is a city with a land area of 527,000 hectares and a total area of 527 square kilometers. It has a population of 2,739,551 and a population density of 5,165.1 people per square kilometer. The city is situated at an elevation of 2,354.8848 meters above sea level and is located in the East Africa Time zone, with a UTC offset of +3. Addis Ababa is the capital of Ethiopia and serves as one of the country's regions. The city was founded by Menelik II and Taytu Betul. Addis Ababa is home to several notable locations, including Menelik II School, Betoch, Dembel City Center, and the sites of significant historical events such as the Battle of Segale, the 1989 Ethiopian coup d'état attempt, and the 1960 Ethiopian coup d'état attempt. The city is also associated with several individuals, including Rophnan, Sayat Demissie, Meron Getnet, Caleb Meakins, Belay Zeleke, and Dawit Nega, who were either born or died there. Historically, Addis Ababa served as the capital of the Derg regime, the People's Democratic Republic of Ethiopia, and the Transitional Government of Ethiopia. The city is also a significant location for industrial activities, with companies like Tofaş Şahin and Hyundai Ioniq having assembly plants there. Educational institutions such as Unity University and Royal College, Addis Abeba, have campuses in the city. Addis Ababa is the headquarters of several organizations, including the Development Bank of Ethiopia, the United Ethiopian Democratic Forces, and the Prosperity Party. The city is also the hometown of notable figures like Endegna, Walias Band, and Getatchew Mekurya. Enat Bank and Metals and Engineering Corporation are among the companies located in the city. The city is the residence of several prominent individuals, including Oumer Hussein, Ahmed Shide, and Abune Mathias. Addis Ababa is also the garrison of military units such as Mehal Sefari, the 65th Infantry Division "Granatieri di Savoia," and Kebur Zabagna. The city is home to sports teams like Defence Force S.C., Ethio Electric S.C., and Saint George S.C. Additionally, Hizkias Assefa is associated with the city through his education.
Adelaide, a city in Australia, has a total population of 1,387,290. Located in Adelaide are Castle Plaza, Prescott Schools, and the setting of the film *Sam Fox: Extreme Adventures*. Several notable individuals were born in Adelaide, including Cameron Williams, a cricketer, Carl Tietjens, and Carlee Taylor. Additionally, Carl Linger, Pāvils Dreijmanis, and Quentin Kenihan passed away in Adelaide.
Ahmedabad, a metropolis in India, boasts an urban area of 1,866 square kilometers and a total area of 505 square kilometers. With a population exceeding 8.5 million, it is a bustling city governed by the Amdavad Municipal Corporation under a mayor–council system. The city's elevation is 53 meters, and its residents are known as Ahmedabadi or Amdavadi. Ahmedabad operates under the Indian Standard Time zone with a UTC offset of +5:30 and uses the postal code 380 0XX. Prominent landmarks in Ahmedabad include the Calico Dome and Sanskar Kendra, while the Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel International Airport serves as a key transportation hub. The city is also home to the Entrepreneurship Development Institute of India and Smt. NHL Municipal Medical College. Notable individuals such as Amit Dave, Pradipsinh Jadeja, and Priti Sengupta were born in Ahmedabad, while others like Prahalad Chunnilal Vaidya and Pranlal Kharsani passed away there. Ahmedabad's educational landscape includes institutions attended by figures like Nikhil Paramjit Sharma and Disha Vakani. The city hosts the 11th Indian Infantry Division and the Gujarat Titans sports team. It is a manufacturing hub for Suzuki vehicles and the headquarters for organizations like Bochasanwasi Akshar Purushottam Swaminarayan Sanstha and media outlets such as DD Girnar and Colors Gujarati. The region serves various services, including medical care at SVP Hospital and Ahmedabad Civil Hospital, and transport through Ahmedabad Municipal Transport Service. Businesses like MylesCar and Jasuben Pizza operate here, catering to the local population. Notable residents include Pradip Parmar, Rengaswamy Ramesh, and Mavji Desai, contributing to the city's vibrant community.
Algiers, the capital of Algeria, is a city rich in history and culture. With a total area of 363 square kilometers and a metropolitan area spanning 1,190 square kilometers, Algiers is home to a population of approximately 4,510,000 residents, giving it a population density of 12,424 people per square kilometer in the city proper and 7,012 people per square kilometer in the metropolitan area. The city is served by the area code (+213) 021 and features postal codes ranging from 16000 to 16132. Located in the Central European Time zone, Algiers operates on a UTC offset of +01:00. Algiers is not only the political capital but also a hub for education and culture. Prestigious institutions such as the University of Science and Technology Houari Boumediene and the National Polytechnic School are situated here. The city is also home to the Supreme Council of the Arabic Language in Algeria, underscoring its linguistic and cultural significance. The city's historical importance is evident from events like the Capture of Peñón of Algiers in 1529 and the Battle of Algiers during 1956–1957. Additionally, the Battle of Bab El Oued is another significant historical event associated with Algiers. Algiers boasts a vibrant cultural scene, with the Sanaa music style originating from the city. The Botanical Garden Hamma and the Renault Dauphine assembly plant are notable landmarks and industrial sites. The city has hosted several Algerian Cup Finals in 2010, 2011, and 2012, showcasing its role in national sports events. Several organizations and institutions have their headquarters in Algiers, including the Electricity and Gas Regulation Commission, the Provisional Government of the Algerian Republic, and the Democratic National Rally. Media outlets like Samira TV and the Algeria Press Service are also based here. The city is a garrison for the Republican Guard and the Algerian Land Forces, highlighting its strategic importance. Algiers is the birthplace of notable figures such as Roger Hanin, Samira Negrouche, and Baya El Hachemi. It is also the final resting place for individuals like Saïd Bouhadja, Léon Carré, and Léon Cauvy. The city's influence extends to architecture, with John McAslan having designed significant buildings there. Residents of Algiers include Adam Larfi and Inès Ibbou, while notable individuals like Amel Brahim-Djelloul, Biyouna, and Julie Pietri call the city their hometown. The Mediterranean Sea is nearest to Algiers, and the city is also associated with the Canary Islands Independence Movement, which has its headquarters there. Henry Stanyford Blanckley is noted for his occupation in Algiers, and the traditional dish Tajine Mtewem originates from the region. Jean-Baptiste Nouvion is recorded as having a spouse in Algiers, further illustrating the city's diverse connections.
Almaty, the largest city in Kazakhstan, boasts a metropolitan area of 9,395 square kilometers and a total area of 682 square kilometers. With a population of approximately 1,977,011 residents, it serves as a significant urban center. The city is located in the UTC+6 time zone and can be reached via the area code +7 727. Almaty is governed by the Almaty City Mäslihat and is classified as part of the list of cities in Kazakhstan. Notable landmarks and locations within Almaty include the President's Residence, the Satbayev Memorial Museum, Sayran Lake, and the historic site of Jeltoqsan. The city is also the birthplace of several prominent individuals, such as Roman Chentsov, Roman Kirsch, and Sanzhar Mustafin. Additionally, Almaty has been the final resting place for figures like Boris Blinov, Boris Katalymov, and Uzakbay Karamanov. The city is further associated with the notable work of Yesken Sergebayev. Transportation in Almaty is served by Bek Air, which targets the city as its primary airport. Historically, Almaty served as the capital of the Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic. The city is also a hub for manufacturing, with the assembly of the Hyundai H350 taking place there. Media presence includes Qazaq Radiosy, which operates in the city. Educational institutions in Almaty include Satbayev University, a prominent center for higher learning. The city has hosted significant events, such as the 2013 Asian Shotgun Championships. Politically, Almaty was the site of the 2021 Almaty City Mäslihat election and serves as the headquarters for several political parties, including the Rukhaniyat Party and the Democratic Party Adilet. Military presence in Almaty is evident through the Central Asian Military District, the Central Military Band of the Ministry of Defense of Kazakhstan, and the Internal Troops of Kazakhstan, all of which have garrisons in the city. Sports are well-represented, with football clubs like AFC Kairat, FC Alma-Ata, and FC Megasport based there. Prime Aviation and several political parties, including the Democratic Party Adilet, have their headquarters in Almaty. Culturally, Almaty is home to the Holy Dragons and is the hometown of individuals like Liza Umarova and Deniz Reno. The city's proximity to natural attractions such as Big Almaty Lake, Shymbulak, and Charyn National Park makes it a popular destination. Almaty Arena, operated by the city, is a key venue for various events. Notable residents include Zarina Diyas, Timur Khabibulin, and Aleksandr Nedovyesov. Administratively, Almaty encompasses districts like Medeu District and Akbulak. The city's diverse offerings, from education and culture to sports and natural beauty, make it a vibrant and significant urban center in Kazakhstan.
Amman, the capital of Jordan, is a city rich in history and modern significance. With a total area of 1,680 square kilometers and a population of over 4,061,150, it boasts a high population density of 2,380 people per square kilometer. The city is served by the area code +962(6) and features postal codes ranging from 11110 to 17198. Amman is situated in the UTC+3 time zone and is the capital of Jordan, a distinction it also held during the Emirate of Transjordan and the Jordanian annexation of the West Bank. The city is home to numerous cultural and educational institutions, such as the Campbell Gray Living, the Amman Center for Human Rights Studies, and the Princess Sumaya University for Technology. It hosts events like the Amman Stand-up Comedy Festival and is associated with historical battles, including the First Battle of Amman and the Battle of Nablus (1918). Amman has been the birthplace of notable figures like Rouzbahan Fraij, Sama'a Khraisat, Sami al-Oraydi, and the death place of individuals such as Behnam Abu Alsoof, Samir Al-Rifai, and Samir Ghawshah. The city's infrastructure includes key healthcare facilities like Jordan Hospital, Specialty Hospital, Prince Hamza Hospital, Arab Medical Center, and the King Hussein Cancer Center. It is also served by Queen Alia International Airport, a major transportation hub. Amman is the headquarters for organizations like the American Center of Research, Ammon News, and Roya TV, and is the garrison location for the Royal Jordanian Air Force, Royal Jordanian Army, and the 3rd Armored Division. Amman's cultural scene is vibrant, with hometown bands like JadaL, El Morabba3, and Akher Zapheer. It is the residence of notable individuals such as Bayan Tal, Julyana Al-Sadeq, and Lina Attel. The city's economy is supported by companies like Zara Investment Holding, Jobedu, and Tamatem Games, and it has been a location for assembly by Lada Niva. Amman's historical significance is further marked by its association with figures like Zubayr ibn al-Awwam and Henri Vanwaetermeulen, who were involved in battles in the city.
Amsterdam, the capital of the Netherlands, covers a total area of 219.32 square kilometers, comprising 165,760,000 square meters of land and 53,560,000 square meters of water. The city is situated at an elevation of -2 meters below sea level. With a population of 907,976 residents, Amsterdam is a significant urban center. The city is reachable via the area code 020 and has postal codes ranging from 1000 to 1183. Amsterdam operates on Central European Time (CET) and observes daylight saving time as Central European Summer Time (CEST), with UTC offsets of +1 and +2, respectively. The city's motto, "Heldhaftig, Vastberaden, Barmhartig," translates to "Valiant, Steadfast, Compassionate," reflecting its historical and cultural identity. Governed by a municipal council, Amsterdam is classified as one of the municipalities of the Netherlands and holds the distinction of being the nation's capital. Amsterdam is home to several notable institutions and landmarks, including the Amsterdam Museum and the Press Museum. The Prins Hendrikkade is a prominent location within the city. Historically, Amsterdam has been the site of significant events such as the Bijltjesoproer, the Anabaptist riot, and Operation Ramrod 16. The city has also been the birthplace of several individuals, including Calvin Jong-a-Pin, Calvin Mac-Intosch, and Calvin Valies. Additionally, Amsterdam has been the final resting place for figures such as Cab Kaye, Caesar ten Cate, and Carel Victor Gerritsen.
Ankara, the capital of Turkey, is a city rich in history, culture, and significance. With an urban area of 2,767.85 square kilometers and a total area of 24,521 square kilometers, Ankara is home to a population of 5,747,325 people, giving it a metropolitan density of 234 individuals per square kilometer. Residents of Ankara are known as Ankaran, and the city is reachable via postal codes starting with 06xxx and an area code of 1. Historical sites such as the Roman Baths of Ankara are also located here. The city has been a backdrop for significant historical events, including the 1962 Turkish coup attempt, the Battle of Ancyra, and the Siege of Ankara. Companies such as GAMA Enerji and Turkish Aerospace Industries operate in Ankara, which is also where vehicles like the MAN Lion's City and Neoplan Skyliner are assembled. Ankara's residents include prominent individuals like Philip S. Kosnett, Beytullah Kayışdağ, Sadık Savaş, and Salih Aydın. The city hosted the 2012 Turkish Cup Final and is where Osman Kavala pursued his education. With its blend of history, culture, and modern significance, Ankara stands as a vital city in Turkey.

Bamako, the capital and largest city of Mali, is situated in West Africa and serves as the nation's administrative and economic hub. With an elevation of 350 meters above sea level, Bamako spans a total area of 245 square kilometers and boasts a metropolitan area of 17,141.6 square kilometers. The city is home to a population of approximately 2,713,000 residents, with a metropolitan population of 2,757,234 and a high population density of 7,384.11 people per square kilometer in the city proper, and 160.85 people per square kilometer in the metropolitan area. Bamako has been a significant location for key historical events, including the 1968 and 1991 Malian coups d'état. The city is also the birthplace of notable individuals such as Roger Antoine, Samba Ousemane Sow, and Samba Sow, a footballer born in 1989. Additionally, Bamako has been the final resting place for several prominent figures, including Baréma Bocoum, Garan Fabou Kouyate, and Modibo Keita, who was born in 1942. The city is home to several important landmarks and institutions. The Pavillon des Sports Modibo Keita and the Sacred Heart Cathedral are prominent structures in Bamako. Modibo Keita International Airport serves as a key transportation hub, and the city is a target airport for airlines such as Eagle Air (Guinea) and Sky Mali. Bamako is also the location of the University of Bamako and the Mandé Bukari University, as well as the venue for the 2002 Africa Cup of Nations Final. Sports play a significant role in the city, with teams like Djoliba AC, AS Real Bamako, and Atar Club based there. Politically, Bamako hosts the headquarters of the Democratic Union of the Malian People and the United Nations Multidimensional Integrated Stabilization Mission in Mali. The city is also the headquarters of Douniah Airlines and the location of Aéroports du Mali and Sotelma. Culturally, Bamako is the hometown of renowned artists such as Vieux Farka Touré, Trio Da Kali, and Amadou & Mariam. The city is also where Bamako Sign Language is spoken. Historically, Bamako served as the capital of the French Sudan and the Upper Senegal and Niger territories. In its vicinity lies the Badinko Faunal Reserve, the nearest city to this protected area.

Bridgetown, the capital of Barbados and the British Windward Islands, is a city rich in history and culture. With a total area of approximately 38.85 square kilometers and an elevation of just 1 meter above sea level, Bridgetown is home to a population of around 110,000 residents. The city operates on Atlantic Standard Time, with a UTC offset of -4 hours, and can be reached via the area code +1 246. As the capital, Bridgetown is not only the political heart of Barbados but also a hub for education and culture. The University of the West Indies at Cave Hill and Erdiston Teachers' Training College are both located in the city, contributing to its intellectual and academic vibrancy. Additionally, Bridgetown is home to the historic Garrison Historic Area, a UNESCO World Heritage Site, and the House of Assembly of Barbados, reflecting its significant role in the island's governance and history. The city is also a center for various organizations and institutions. The Barbados Labour Party has its headquarters in Bridgetown, and the city serves as the base for beauty pageants such as Miss Barbados World and Miss Universe Barbados. Furthermore, Bridgetown is the headquarters for Bajan Helicopters, which offers aerial services, and the location of the Bridgetown Heliport, providing additional transportation options. Bridgetown's cultural influence extends beyond its shores. The song "Hate That I Love You" was recorded in the city, showcasing its role in the music industry. The city is also home to several sports teams, including Notre Dame SC, Combined Campuses and Colleges cricket team, and Ellerton FC, all of which use Bridgetown as their ground. The city's significance is further highlighted by its proximity to notable geographical features. Carlisle Bay, Barbados, and the Caribbean Sea are both nearest to Bridgetown, underscoring its strategic coastal location. Bridgetown has been the birthplace or residence of several notable individuals. Cameron Chesterfield Alleyne, Roshon Gittens, Roshon Primus, and Darian King were all born in the city, while Campbell Foster, Roger Blades, and Denys Williams passed away there. Additionally, Anthony Forde, a darts player, and Alison Hinds, a renowned artist, call Bridgetown their hometown. Meagan Best, a prominent figure, also resides in the city. In summary, Bridgetown is a city of historical, cultural, and educational significance, serving as the capital of Barbados and the British Windward Islands. Its rich history, vibrant culture, and strategic location make it a focal point of activity and influence in the region.
Brisbane, a city in Australia, has a total population of 2,582,007. It is home to several notable organizations and individuals. Cambia, a non-profit organization, is located in Brisbane, as is Canterbury College in Waterford and Castlemaine Perkins. The city is also the birthplace of Caitlin Sargent-Jones, Cameron Ambridge, and Cameron Bairstow. Additionally, Brisbane is where Carol Burns, Robert Mulvey, and Robert Sayers passed away.
Brussels, the capital of Belgium, boasts a metropolitan population of 2,500,000 and covers a total area of 162.4 square kilometers. With an elevation of 13 meters, it was founded on June 18, 1989. The city is home to 1,222,637 residents and utilizes 42 postal codes. Brussels operates on Central European Time and Central European Summer Time, with UTC offsets of +1 and +2. It is categorized as part of Belgium's communities, regions, and language areas. Several notable organizations are based in Brussels, including Caritas Europa, Carnegie Endowment for International Peace, and Befimmo. Historically, the city was the site of the Battle of Anderlecht and the Siege of Brussels. It is also the birthplace of prominent figures such as Camille Gutt, Camille Japy, and Camille van Mulders. Additionally, Brussels is where Camille Gutt, Camille Janssen, and Camille Van den Plas passed away.
Bucharest, the capital of Romania, is a city rich in history and culture. With a total population of 1,883,425 and a metropolitan population of 2,341,673, it covers an area of 240 square kilometers. The city's metropolitan area spans 1,804 square kilometers, with a population density of 1,298 people per square kilometer in the metro area and 7,621 in the city proper. Situated at an elevation of 55.8 meters, Bucharest is known for its motto, "Patria și dreptul meu," which translates to "The Homeland and my right." Bucharest operates under a mayor–council government and observes Eastern European Time, with UTC offsets of +02:00 and +03:00. The city is home to notable landmarks such as Calea Victoriei, Carlton Bloc, and Carol Park. Historically, Bucharest has been the site of significant events, including the Battle of Bucharest, the Battle of the Argeș, and the Bombing of Bucharest during World War II. The city has also been the birthplace and final resting place of several notable individuals. Cabral Ibacka, Calin Rovinescu, and Camil Petrescu were born in Bucharest, while figures like Cabiria Andreian Cazacu, Caius Iacob, and Camil Petrescu also passed away there. This blend of history, culture, and notable figures makes Bucharest a vibrant and significant city in Romania.
Budapest, the capital of Hungary, was founded on November 17, 1873. The city spans a total area of 525.2 square kilometers, with a metropolitan area of 7,626 square kilometers and an urban area of 2,538 square kilometers. As of the latest data, Budapest has a total population of 1,752,286 residents, with a metropolitan population of 3,011,598. The population density is approximately 3,388 people per square kilometer. Situated at an elevation of 96 meters above sea level, Budapest is characterized by its diverse landscape. Administratively, Budapest is governed by the General Assembly of Budapest and operates under the time zones of Central European Time (UTC+1) and Central European Summer Time (UTC+2). The city is reachable via the area code 1 and has postal codes ranging from 1011 to 1239. Notable institutions and events associated with Budapest include the Capital Circus of Budapest, the Presidential Council of the Hungarian People's Republic, the Promontor utcai Stadion, and significant historical events such as the Battle of the Corvin Passage, the Siege of Budapest, and the Budapest offensive. Budapest is also notable for its connection to several prominent individuals. Camilla von Hollay was both born and died in the city, while Camille Sandorfy and Carl Schultz were born there. Additionally, Carl Schlechter and Carl von Than passed away in Budapest. This rich tapestry of history, administration, and culture makes Budapest a city of significant importance and character.
Buenos Aires, the capital and an autonomous city of Argentina, covers a land area of 203 square kilometers and has a metropolitan area spanning 4,757,808 square kilometers. With a metropolitan population of 15,624,000, it is a bustling urban center. The city is situated at an elevation of 24.9936 meters above sea level and operates on time zones UTC-3 and UTC-2. Founded on February 2, 1536, Buenos Aires is governed by the Buenos Aires City Legislature under an autonomous city government type. Notable landmarks include the historic Cabildo of Buenos Aires, the renowned Café Tortoni, and the popular California Burrito Co. The city has been the site of significant historical events such as the Battle of Miserere, the Bombing of Plaza de Mayo, and the Revolution of 11 September 1852. Buenos Aires is also the birthplace of notable figures like Cacho Castaña, Cacho Fontana, and Camila Crescimbeni, and the final resting place of Cacho Castaña, Cacho Fontana, and Caesar Augustus Rodney. The city’s area code is 011, and it is a major cultural and economic hub in Argentina.
Bujumbura, the capital and largest city of Burundi, covers an urban area of 127 square kilometers and is situated at an elevation of 774 meters above sea level. With a population of approximately one million residents, the city serves as a significant urban center in the region. Bujumbura operates on Central Africa Time, with a UTC offset of +2 hours, and is the administrative hub of Burundi, historically serving as the capital during the Kingdom of Burundi and the earlier Ruanda-Urundi period. The city is home to several notable landmarks and institutions, including the Regina Mundi Cathedral, the University of Burundi, and Bujumbura International Airport. It also hosts the headquarters of the Authority for Regulation of Water and Energy Sectors and the Burundi Red Cross. The city’s vibrant cultural scene is enriched by the presence of media outlets like Urunani BBC and BeTV (Burundi). Bujumbura is associated with several prominent individuals, such as Sat-B, Bienvenue Kanakimana, and Bonfils-Caleb Bimenyimana, who were born in the city, while figures like Venant Bacinoni, Melchior Ndadaye, and Emmanuel Niyonkuru have ties to Bujumbura as their place of death. The city is also the hometown of Spoks Man, a notable public figure. Sports enthusiasts in Bujumbura support local football clubs such as Prince Louis FC, Vital'O FC, and Muzinga FC, which are based in the city. Additionally, Bujumbura is the nearest major city to Rusizi National Park and the scenic Lake Tanganyika, making it a gateway to these natural attractions.

Caracas, the capital and largest city of Venezuela, is a vibrant metropolis with a rich history and diverse cultural landscape. Established on July 25, 1567, by founder Diego de Losada, the city spans a total area of 433 square kilometers and boasts a metropolitan area of 4,715.1 square kilometers. Situated at an elevation of 900 meters above sea level, Caracas is home to a population of approximately 2,956,813 residents. The city operates under a Mayor–council government and is governed by a list of Venezuela governors, maintaining a Venezuelan Standard Time Zone with a UTC offset of −4. Caracas is renowned for its significant landmarks and cultural contributions. The city is home to the Bolivarian Military University of Venezuela and other esteemed institutions such as the Universidad Alejandro de Humboldt and the Universidad Metropolitana. Notable individuals like Canserbero, Carla Arocha, and Carlos Ascues were born in Caracas, while others, such as Carlos Alberto Taylhardat and Carlos Augusto León, have passed away there. The city also hosts various organizations, including the Bolivarian Militia of Venezuela and the Bolivarian Intelligence Service. Transportation in Caracas is facilitated by companies like Air Nicaragua, which targets the city’s airport, and automotive assembly plants for models such as the Chevrolet Camaro and AMC Javelin. The city’s infrastructure includes the Cabletren Bolivariano and notable streets like Calle Luna and Calle Sol. Caracas is also a hub for media and entertainment, with recordings of songs like "El Cariño Es Como Una Flor" and "No Basta" taking place there. Sports enthusiasts will find teams such as Deportivo Galicia, Deportivo La Guaira F.C., and Deportivo Petare F.C. based in Caracas. The city’s educational landscape is further enriched by institutions like the Universidad Nueva Esparta. Caracas is also the headquarters for organizations like Progressive Advance and the Bolivarian Army of Trolls, showcasing its diverse administrative and cultural roles. In summary, Caracas is a city steeped in history, education, and culture, serving as a vital center for governance, transportation, and entertainment in Venezuela.

Damascus, the capital of Syria, boasts an urban area of 77,000,000 square meters and a total area of 105 square kilometers. Situated at an elevation of 680 meters above sea level, the city has a population of approximately 2,503,000 residents and is located in the UTC+3 time zone. Damascus is not only the largest city in Syria but also serves as the capital of the Syrian opposition. The city is home to several government ministries, including the Ministry of Agriculture and Agrarian Reform, the Ministry of Communications and Technology, and the Ministry of Expatriates, all of which have their headquarters there. Historically, Damascus has been a significant location for various events. The Capture of Damascus in 1920 and the Qaboun offensive in 2017 are notable historical incidents that took place in the city. Additionally, Damascus has been the capital of several historical entities, such as the Umayyad Caliphate, the Arab Kingdom of Syria, and Aram-Damascus. The city has also served as a garrison for military units, including the Republican Guard and the VIII Corps of the Ottoman Empire. Culturally, Damascus is a vibrant city. It hosted the Pan Arab Games in both 1976 and 1992. The city is associated with the Western Neo-Aramaic language and is the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Caresse Bashar, Ammar Abd Rabbo, and Qadri Jamil. Damascus is also the residence of prominent figures like Bassam Tohme and Salam Safaf. Damascus has been a significant location for various industries and events. The IKCO Samand is assembled in the city, and it has been a battleground for historical conflicts, such as the 17th Horse (Poona Horse) battle. The city is also associated with the assembly of the 17th Horse (Poona Horse) and has been the setting for works like "The Mirrors of Fire." Damascus continues to be a central hub for governance, culture, and history in Syria.

The city is densely populated, with a population density of 11,312.02 individuals per square kilometer and a total population of 16,787,941 residents. Situated at an elevation of 198.12 meters above sea level, Delhi operates on Indian Standard Time, with a UTC offset of +5:30. As a union territory, it is governed by the Government of Delhi. Delhi is home to several notable establishments, including the Pragati-III Combined Cycle Power Plant and the Pragati-I Combined Cycle Gas Power Station, which contribute to the city's energy needs. Additionally, the Punjab National Bank has a presence in Delhi, highlighting its significance in the financial sector. Historically, Delhi has been a site of significant events. The Capture of Delhi in 1771 and the Battle of Badli-ki-Serai are notable historical occurrences that took place in the city. Furthermore, the Battle of Delhi in 1757 is another important event in its historical landscape. Delhi has also been the birthplace of several notable individuals. Amit Sharma, a director, Prabh Deep, a musician, and Prachi Tehlan, an actress, all trace their origins to this vibrant city. Moreover, Delhi has been the final resting place for prominent figures such as Camille Bulcke, the late Pranab Mukherjee, and Prateek Chaudhuri, who passed away in the city.
Dhaka, the capital of Bangladesh, is a bustling metropolis with a metropolitan area of 2,161,168,958.883889 square kilometers and an urban area of 305,470,000 square kilometers. The city is home to a population of 21,741,090 in its metropolitan area, with a high population density of 29,373 people per square kilometer. Dhaka is situated at an elevation of 31.991808 meters above sea level and operates on Bangladesh Standard Time, with a UTC offset of +6. The city is divided into several postal zones, including 1000, 1100, 12xx, and 13xx. Dhaka is governed by the Dhaka North City Corporation and the Dhaka South City Corporation, operating under a Mayor-Council government system. As the capital, it serves as the administrative and economic hub of Bangladesh. The city is home to numerous educational institutions, including the Royal University of Dhaka, Gono University, Government Saadat College, and the Government College of Applied Human Science. Additionally, the Institute of Cost and Management Accountants of Bangladesh and the Canadian University of Bangladesh also have campuses in Dhaka. The city's economy is supported by various industries and organizations. The Bengal Commercial Bank Limited and Pubali Bank are headquartered in Dhaka, and the Bengal Group of Industries operates from the city. The Progressive Democratic Party of Bangladesh also has its headquarters there. Dhaka is a significant location for transportation and infrastructure, with the Purbachal Expressway and the assembly of the Toyota Corolla (E120) model taking place within the city. Dhaka has a rich cultural and historical significance. It was the capital of the Bengal Subah during the Mughal Empire and has been the site of several historical events, including the Bangladesh Rifles revolt and the 3 November 1975 Bangladeshi coup d'état. The city is also the birthplace of notable individuals such as Prafulla Chandra Ghosh, Prafulla Roy, and Prarthana Fardin Dighi. Additionally, Dhaka has been the deathplace of prominent figures like Begum Feroza Bari, Qayyum Chowdhury, and Qazi Abdul Alim. In terms of architecture, Dhaka is notable for the work of Brian MacKay-Lyons, who has designed significant buildings in the city. The Royal Bengal Airline has its hub airport in Dhaka, and the city is a key location for military operations, with the Counter Terrorism and Intelligence Bureau, Bangladesh Naval Aviation, and Bangladesh Navy maintaining a presence there. Sports and education are also prominent in Dhaka. The city is home to the Bangladesh national under-19 cricket team and serves as the ground for several sports seasons, including the 2019–20 Bangladesh Police FC season and the 2020–21 Abahani Limited Dhaka season. The city's educational landscape includes institutions like the Bangladesh Home Economics College and Presidency University, Bangladesh, as well as Prime University and the education of notable figures like Shayan Chowdhury Arnob. Dhaka's significance extends to its role in governance and public services. The Cabinet Committee on Public Purchase is headquartered in the city, and the Bangladesh Naval Aviation and Bangladesh Navy maintain a garrison there. Overall, Dhaka is a vibrant city that blends historical richness with modern development, serving as the heart of Bangladesh's political, economic, and cultural activities.

This blend of history, culture, and geography makes Guayaquil a vibrant and multifaceted city.

Harare, the capital of Zimbabwe, is a city rich in history, culture, and modern significance. With a metropolitan population of 3,120,917 and a total area of 940 square kilometers, Harare stands as the largest city in Zimbabwe and formerly in the Federation of Rhodesia and Nyasaland. Established on April 18, 1982, the city is situated at an elevation of 1,490 meters and operates under a Mayor-council government. Harare is in the Central Africa Time zone with a UTC offset of +2 and is reachable via area code 242. The city's historical significance is marked by its role as the capital of Rhodesia and Rhodesia (1964–1965), and during the company rule in Rhodesia. The Parliament of Rhodesia and Morgan Tsvangirai House are notable landmarks, while the 2017 Zimbabwean coup d'état took place within its borders. Harare is also the final resting place for figures like Protais Mpiranya, Rodney Gordon, and Ronald Wilson. Economically, Harare has been a hub for manufacturing, with Ford assembling models like the F-Series (fourth generation) and the Zephyr. Businesses such as Nash Paints, Telecel Zimbabwe, and Oncocare operate within the city, which is also a key location for Sub-Saharan Africa's economic activities. Transportation in Harare is facilitated by its role as a target or hub airport for airlines like Air Trans Africa, Air Rhodesia, and Zimbabwe Express Airlines. The city's sports scene is lively, with teams like Black Rhinos F.C., Mashonaland Eagles, and Monomotapa United F.C. based there. Politically and militarily, Harare hosts the headquarters of the Republican Front, Responsible Government Association, and Rhodesia Prison Service, along with garrisons for the Presidential Guard, Rhodesian Armoured Corps, and Rhodesian Light Infantry. The city is also the hometown of musicians Roki, Mizchif, and Mudiwa Hood, adding to its cultural vibrancy. Notable residents include David Parirenyatwa, Humphrey Gibbs, and Paul Tangi Mhova Mkondo, reflecting Harare's diverse and influential community. This blend of history, culture, and modernity makes Harare a significant urban center in Zimbabwe and the region.

It was also the capital of the Provisional Revolutionary Government of the Republic of South Vietnam. In summary, Ouagadougou is a vibrant city that blends historical significance with modern infrastructure, serving as a cultural, political, and economic center in Burkina Faso.

The city is easily accessible with its area code (+359) 02 and postal code 1000. Sofia operates on Eastern European Time (EET) and Eastern European Summer Time (EEST), with UTC offsets of +2 and +3, respectively. The city's residents are known as Sofians, or Софиянец/Sofiyanets in Bulgarian, reflecting the city's diverse linguistic heritage. Sofia's motto, "Ever growing, never aging," encapsulates its enduring spirit, also expressed in Bulgarian as "Расте, но не старее." Sofia's strategic location has made it a focal point for various historical events. The 1923 Bulgarian coup d'état, the Battle of Sofia, and the Siege of Serdica in 809 are testament to its historical significance. The city is home to notable landmarks and organizations such as Capital Fort, Powernet, and Pravetz Computers, highlighting its modern infrastructure and technological advancements. Prominent individuals like Preslav Borissov and Preslav Borukov were born in Sofia, while others, including Pravoslav Tenev and Rumen Apostolov, have passed away there. These connections underscore Sofia's role as a place of birth, life, and legacy for many influential figures. Sofia's blend of historical depth and contemporary vibrancy makes it a unique and dynamic city.

Valletta, the capital of Malta, is a city rich in history and culture. Established in 1566 by Jean Parisot de Valette, it was built as a fortress city by the Knights Hospitaller. The city's motto, "City Built By Gentlemen For Gentlemen," reflects its noble origins. Valletta is situated on the northeast coast of Malta, with an elevation of 56 meters above sea level. It covers an urban area of 256 hectares and a total area of 0.61 square kilometers, with a population of 5,827 residents as of the latest census. Valletta has been the capital during various periods of Maltese history, including under the Hospitaller Malta, the Crown Colony of Malta, and the French occupation. The city's time zone is Central European Time, with UTC+1 in winter and UTC+2 in summer. The postal code for Valletta is VLT, and the area code is 356. It has also been the final resting place for figures like Vincenzo Dimech, Anastasio Cuschieri, and Mattia Preti. Valletta's significance extends beyond its historical roots; it is also a center for media, with radio stations like Capital Radio Malta and One Radio operating from the city. Valletta is the headquarters of the Ministry for Foreign and European Affairs of Malta and has been the residence of various prominent individuals, including Pawlu Camilleri, Jes Psaila, and Boris Pašanski. The city's cultural influence is further evident in its educational institutions, such as the one attended by Giovanni Pietro Francesco Agius de Soldanis. Valletta's garrison has historically been associated with the Knights Hospitaller and the Navy of the Order of Saint John, underscoring its military and strategic importance. In addition to its historical and cultural landmarks, Valletta is home to the Monte della Redenzione degli Schiavi and the Journal de Malte. The city's vibrant community includes residents like Emmanuel Mallia and Angelo Portelli, and it has been the hometown of Manwel Dimech and Nicholas Zammit. Valletta United W.P.C. has its stadium in the city, adding to its sporting culture. The French frigate Carthaginoise was built in Valletta, highlighting its historical shipbuilding significance. The city's diverse influences and rich history make it a unique and fascinating place.

With a population of 453 residents, the city-state boasts a high population density of 924 individuals per square kilometer. Italian is the official language, though Latin is also spoken. Several individuals, including Carlo Cremonesi, Egidio Vagnozzi, and Gennaro Granito Pignatelli di Belmonte, have passed away within its borders. The Holy See designates Vatican City as its capital. Pastine International Airport and Leonardo da Vinci–Fiumicino Airport serve the area. Media and institutions such as Boomerang TV channel, Annuario Pontificio, Vatican Library, Swiss Guard, Vatican Apostolic Archive, Vatican News, Acta Apostolicae Sedis, Vatican Pharmacy, Vatican Media, Istituto Poligrafico e Zecca dello Stato, RAI, and Sky Italia operate within or serve Vatican City. Prominent residents include Audrys Bačkis, José Gabriel Funes, Georges Cottier, and Fernando Filoni.
Vienna, the capital of Austria, is a city rich in history and culture. With a total area of 395,250,000 square meters, Vienna comprises 19,390,000 square meters of water. The metropolitan area is home to approximately 2,890,577 residents, creating a population density of 4,326.1 people per square kilometer. The city's elevation is 150.876 meters above sea level, and its airport is assigned the postal code 1300. Vienna operates on Central European Summer Time and Central European Time, with UTC offsets of +1 and +2, respectively. As both a capital city and one of Austria's states, Vienna is governed by the Gemeinderat and Landtag. The city is also recognized as a municipality within Austria. Notable landmarks include the Prater, the Presidential Chancellery, and the grand Schönbrunn Palace. Historically, Vienna has been the site of significant battles such as the Battle of Aspern-Essling, the Battle of Schwechat, and the Battle of Vienna. Vientiane, the capital of Laos, is a city rich in history and culture. The city operates on UTC+7 time and is classified as part of the list of cities in Laos. Historically, Vientiane has served as the capital for various entities, including the Lan Xang kingdom, the French protectorate of Laos, and the Kingdom of Laos. It was also the capital of the Royal Lao Government in Exile. The city has been the site of significant events, such as the Battle of Vientiane and the coups of 1960 and 1964. Vientiane is a hub for various institutions and organizations. The city has also hosted notable events, including the 2012 South East Asian Table Tennis Championships and the 2009 Southeast Asian Games. The Royal Lao Air Force, Royal Lao Army Airborne, and Royal Lao Navy also have a presence here. In summary, Vientiane is a city with a rich history, serving as the capital for various regimes and hosting numerous significant events. It is home to important institutions, notable individuals, and a variety of cultural and sports activities, making it a vibrant and multifaceted urban center in Laos.
Warsaw, the capital of Poland, is a city with a rich history and vibrant culture. Situated in the central-eastern part of the country, Warsaw serves as a significant political, economic, and cultural hub. The city covers a total area of 517.24 square kilometers and has a population of approximately 1,860,281 residents, with a population density of 3,596 people per square kilometer. The metropolitan area of Warsaw spans 6,100.43 square kilometers and is home to around 3,100,844 inhabitants, with a density of 509.1 people per square kilometer. Warsaw is governed by the Warsaw City Council under a mayor–council government system. The city is divided into 18 districts, each with its own unique character and administrative functions. Warsaw operates on Central European Time (CET) and observes daylight saving time, shifting to Central European Summer Time (CEST) during the summer months. The city's postal codes range from 00-001 to 04-999, and the area code for Warsaw is +48 22. The elevation of Warsaw is 78 meters above sea level, and its residents are referred to as Varsovians. The city's motto, "Semper invicta," translates to "Ever invincible" in Latin, reflecting its resilience and historical significance. Warsaw is home to several notable landmarks and cultural institutions. The Carmelite Church, Potocki Palace, and Połczyńska Street are just a few examples of the city's architectural and historical treasures. The city has also been the site of several significant battles, including the Battle of Białołęka, the Battle of Nasielsk, and the Battle of Olszynka Grochowska, which are important chapters in its military history. Warsaw has been the birthplace or final resting place of several notable individuals. Casimir Funk, known for his contributions to science, was born in Warsaw, as were Przemysław Bobak and Przemysław Czyż. The city has also been the deathplace of figures such as Calel Perechodnik, Predrag Đajić, and Przemysław Gintrowski, adding to its rich cultural and historical tapestry.

Yangon, the largest city in Myanmar, boasts a metropolitan area of 10,170 square kilometers and an urban area spanning 598.75 square kilometers. Overall, Yangon's diverse roles as a historical capital, educational center, cultural hub, and modern metropolis underscore its importance in Myanmar.

Yerevan, the capital of Armenia, is a city rich in history and culture. Zagreb, the capital city of Croatia, boasts a diverse range of characteristics that define its urban landscape and cultural significance. Zürich, the largest city in Switzerland, is situated in the canton of Zürich and serves as its capital. The city spans a total area of 91.88 square kilometers and is elevated at 408 meters above sea level. Residents of Zürich are known as Zürcher(in), and the city is divided into various postal code areas ranging from 8000 to 8099. Politically, Zürich is led by the Social Democratic Party of Switzerland, with Corine Mauch serving as the mayor. The city is bordered by neighboring municipalities such as Uitikon, Urdorf, and Maur. Zürich is a significant historical site, having been the location of the First and Second Battles of Zürich, as well as the Army of the Danube's engagement. The city is home to several notable institutions, including the Cantonal Council of Zürich, the historic Carolinum, and the headquarters of the organization Public Eye. Nearby towns like Uster and Wallisellen are also part of the Zürich canton, contributing to the region's diverse landscape. Zürich is also a center for education and culture, hosting institutions such as the University of Zürich, ETH Zürich Faculty of Architecture, and the Swiss magazine Bolero. With its rich history, vibrant culture, and strategic importance, Zürich stands as a significant urban center in Switzerland.
Adam Smith was born in Fife in 1723 and passed away in Edinburgh in 1790. His birth and death dates are recorded as June 5, 1723, and July 17, 1790, respectively. Smith was influenced by prominent thinkers such as Richard Cantillon, Francis Hutcheson, and Aristotle, which shaped his philosophical outlook. He is associated with the Western philosophy tradition. Adam Smith authored two significant works: "The Wealth of Nations" and "The Theory of Moral Sentiments," which are foundational in their fields. Tom Campbell, a philosopher, is linked to Adam Smith in the academic discipline, suggesting a scholarly connection. Additionally, Walter Campbell of Shawfield is noted as Smith's predecessor, indicating a succession or influence in position.
Adolf Hitler was born on April 20, 1889, in Braunau am Inn. He died on April 30, 1945, in Berlin, with his death being part of the events known as the Death of Adolf Hitler. Politically, he was affiliated with both the German Workers' Party and the Nazi Party. Hitler was married to Eva Braun.
Alan Turing was born on June 23, 1912, in Maida Vale and passed away on June 7, 1954, in Wilmslow due to cyanide poisoning. He pursued his academic journey at Princeton University and the University of Cambridge, where he earned a Master of Arts. Turing's doctoral advisor was Alonzo Church, and he, in turn, supervised Robin Gandy and Beatrice Worsley as his doctoral students. His work spanned cryptanalysis, logic, and computer science, earning him the Smith's Prize. Influenced by Max Newman, Turing is renowned for his contributions to the cryptanalysis of the Enigma, Turing's proof, and the Turing test. He also developed Turochamp. His intellectual legacy extends to influencing Jonathan Bowen and Cicely Popplewell.
Albert Einstein was born on March 14, 1879, in Ulm and passed away on April 18, 1955, in Princeton, New Jersey. Throughout his life, he held citizenships in Cisleithania, the Free State of Prussia, and experienced a period of statelessness. Einstein's academic journey was guided by his doctoral advisor, Alfred Kleiner, and he dedicated his career to the field of Physics. His contributions were recognized with notable awards, including the Barnard Medal for Meritorious Service to Science, the Copley Medal, and his membership in the National Academy of Sciences. Einstein's personal life included marriages to Elsa Löwenthal and Mileva Marić, with whom he had children Lieserl, Hans Albert, and Eduard. His work was influenced by Hendrik Lorentz and Hermann Minkowski, and he is renowned for his ensemble interpretation, Bose–Einstein statistics, and the EPR paradox. He authored "The Meaning of Relativity" and was a key figure at the Davos University Conferences. Einstein's legacy extends to influencing scholars like Samarendra Kumar Mitra and appearing in the film "Atomic Power." His impact on science and culture remains profound.
Aleister Crowley, born as Edward Alexander Crowley on October 12, 1875, in Warwickshire, England, passed away on December 1, 1947, in East Sussex. Crowley was a man of diverse pursuits, known as a novelist, mountaineer, and occultist. His educational journey included attendance at Malvern College, Tonbridge School, and Eastbourne College, followed by studies at Trinity College, Cambridge. Crowley's literary contributions are notable, with works such as "Moonchild," "The Blue Equinox," and "777 and Other Qabalistic Writings of Aleister Crowley." His influence extended to several individuals, including Robert Anton Wilson, Lionel Snell, and Wilfred Talbot Smith. In his personal life, Crowley was married to Rose Edith Kelly. His work "The Magical Revival" stands as a subsequent contribution to his legacy.
Alexander Fleming was born on August 6, 1881, in Darvel. He passed away on March 11, 1955. Fleming's academic expertise lay in the fields of bacteriology and immunology. He pursued his education at the University of Westminster, Imperial College London, and St Mary's Hospital Medical School. His contributions to science earned him several prestigious honors, including being named a Fellow of the Royal Society, receiving the Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine, and being appointed a Knight Bachelor. Fleming is most notably recognized for his groundbreaking discovery of penicillin and his earlier work on lysozyme.
Alexander Graham Bell was born in Edinburgh, Scotland, on March 3, 1847, under the name Alexander Bell. He later became a naturalized Canadian. Bell is most renowned for his groundbreaking invention of the telephone, a innovation that revolutionized communication. In addition to his work in telecommunications, he was a pioneer in aviation, designing aircraft such as the Silver Dart and the Cygnet. Bell also played a significant role in founding major corporations, including AT&T Corporation and Bell Canada. He married Mabel Gardiner Hubbard and had children with her. His father, Alexander Melville Bell, was also a prominent figure. Bell passed away on August 2, 1922, in Beinn Bhreagh, Canada, leaving behind a legacy that shaped modern technology and industry.
Alfred Joseph Hitchcock was born on August 13, 1899, in Leytonstone, England. He attended St. Ignatius' College and later studied at Salesian College in Battersea. Hitchcock began his career in the film industry in 1919 and remained active until 1980. He was a renowned film director, producer, and writer, earning numerous awards and nominations throughout his career. Hitchcock married Alma Reville, with whom he had a daughter, Pat Hitchcock. His work spanned various roles, including directing films such as *Psycho* (1960), *Rope* (1948), and *Murder!* (1930). He also produced several films, including *Under Capricorn* (1949) and *Psycho*. Hitchcock's contributions extended to writing, with credits in films like *Blackmail* (1929) and *Rich and Strange* (1931). He was involved in television as well, creating *Alfred Hitchcock Presents*. Hitchcock appeared in documentaries like *Truffaut* (1967) and *The World of Alfred Hitchcock*. He passed away on April 29, 1980, leaving behind a legacy in cinema. C.M. Woolf was notably associated with Hitchcock's career.
Alfred the Great was active from 0871 until 0886. He was the child of Osburh and Æthelwulf, King of Wessex. Alfred married Ealhswith, and they had several children together, including Edward the Elder, Æthelweard, and Ælfthryth, who became the Countess of Flanders. Alfred succeeded his predecessor, Æthelred I, and was later succeeded by his son, Edward the Elder. He was a notable military leader, commanding forces in the Battle of Ashdown, the Battle of Basing, and the Battle of Chippenham.
Ali Mazrui was born in Mombasa, Kenya, on February 24, 1933, and passed away in the United States on October 12, 2014. He was a prominent Kenyan academic, author, and intellectual, active primarily from 1966 until his death in 2014. Mazrui pursued higher education at renowned institutions, including Columbia University, Manchester University, and Oxford University. His contributions earned him state commendations from Kenya, and he was notably recognized for his work on "Black orientalism." Throughout his career, he held various roles, including as an academic and author, leaving a significant impact in his field.
Amartya Sen was born on November 3, 1933, in the British Raj. He pursued his academic journey at the University of Calcutta, where he earned a Master of Arts, and later at Trinity College, Cambridge. Renowned for his contributions, he has received prestigious awards such as the Bharat Ratna, the Johan Skytte Prize in Political Science, and the National Humanities Medal. His work spans development economics, welfare economics, and social choice theory, influenced by notable figures including John Rawls, Mary Wollstonecraft, and Gautama Buddha. Amartya Sen has authored several influential books, including "Development as Freedom," "Inequality Reexamined," and "The Idea of Justice." He is also the founder of the Human Development and Capability Association. In his personal life, he has two children, Antara Dev Sen and Nandana Sen, and was married to Nabaneeta Dev Sen. Additionally, he preceded Martin Rees in a tenure role and appeared in the film "Nobelity." His contributions and recognitions highlight his significant impact in both academia and beyond.
Amos Oz, born as Amos Klausner on May 4, 1939, in Mandatory Palestine, was a prominent Israeli novelist and journalist. He passed away on December 28, 2018, in Petah Tikva. Oz's literary career was marked by notable works such as "My Michael," "A Perfect Peace," and "A Tale of Love and Darkness." His contributions to literature were recognized with several prestigious awards, including the Prince of Asturias Awards, the Bialik Prize, and the Goethe Prize. Additionally, his novel "My Michael" was adapted into a film for which he served as the writer. Amos Oz's legacy endures through his impactful writings and the adaptation of his work into film.
Andrei Sakharov was born in Moscow on May 21, 1921, and passed away in the same city on December 14, 1989. He pursued his academic career under the guidance of Igor Tamm, focusing on Nuclear physics and Physical cosmology. Sakharov earned his education at Moscow State University and the Lebedev Physical Institute. His contributions were recognized with the Elliott Cresson Medal, the Nobel Peace Prize, and the Lenin Prize. Notably, he is known for his work on Proton decay, Electromagnetic pulse, and Baryogenesis. A citizen of the Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic, Sakharov was also a prominent figure in human rights, founding the Committee on Human Rights in the USSR and playing a key role in the Memorial society.
Archimedes, a renowned figure born and deceased in Sicily, excelled in the fields of Mathematics, Mechanics, and Engineering. Influenced by the works of Eudoxus of Cnidus, he made significant contributions to science and technology. Among his notable inventions are Archimedes' principle, which explains buoyancy, the Archimedes' screw, a device for lifting water, and the Lever, a fundamental tool in mechanics. He authored influential works such as "On Floating Bodies" and "On the Equilibrium of Planes." His contributions had a lasting impact, inspiring later thinkers like René Descartes and Gerolamo Cardano.
Aristotle was born in the ancient city of Stagira in the year 384 BCE and passed away in Macedonia in 322 BCE. He was influenced by several prominent figures, including Empedocles, Parmenides, and Hippias. Aristotle is associated with the region of Western philosophy. Manuel Chrysoloras, John Corcoran, and Octavius Freire Owen are notable individuals known for their connection to Aristotle.
Arthur Currie began his military service in 1897 and went on to play a significant role in World War I as part of the Canadian Expeditionary Force. During the war, he distinguished himself as a capable commander, leading troops in several key battles, including the Battle of Hill 70, the Battle of Cambrai in 1918, and the Battle of Amiens in 1918. His contributions were recognized with several awards, including the Croix de guerre from Belgium, the Order of the Crown, also from Belgium, and the French Croix de guerre for the 1914–1918 period. Beyond his military career, Currie was also associated with McGill University and Khaki University, where he held occupational roles. In a different context, Arthur Eustace Morgan is noted as having preceded Currie in a specific tenure.
Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington, was born Arthur Wesley on May 1, 1769, in Dublin. He passed away on September 14, 1852, in Walmer. A prominent figure in both the Conservative Party and the Tory faction, he married Catherine Wellesley, Duchess of Wellington. As a military leader, he constructed the Forts of Alqueidão, Archeira, and Arpim. He commanded significant military engagements, including the Campaign in south-west France in 1814, the Battle of Argaon, and the Battle of Assaye. Beyond his military career, he founded the Carlton Club and was the owner of the horse Copenhagen. He was the father of Arthur Wellesley, 2nd Duke of Wellington. His political career included serving as prime minister during the tenures of John Copley, 1st Baron Lyndhurst, and F.J. Robinson, 1st Viscount Goderich. He was succeeded by John Ponsonby, 4th Earl of Bessborough, and William Lamb, 2nd Viscount Melbourne, in various roles. His legacy endures as a significant historical figure with contributions to both military and political spheres.

Her writing extends to cinema as well, as she contributed to the screenplay of "Electric Moon" and also wrote for "In Which Annie Gives It Those Ones."
Astrid Lindgren, born Astrid Anna Emilia Ericsson on November 14, 1907, in Vimmerby, Sweden, was a renowned author primarily known for her contributions to children's literature. She passed away on January 28, 2002, in Stockholm. Lindgren's active career spanned from 1944 to 2002, during which she created some of the most beloved characters in children's literature. Her works include the books "Mio, My Son," "The Runaway Sleigh Ride," and "Lilibet, Circus Child." She is also celebrated for creating the iconic characters Bill Bergson and Pippi Longstocking. In addition to her literary work, Lindgren contributed to various films, such as "Vi på Saltkråkan," "Pippi in the South Seas," "Ronia, the Robber's Daughter," "Bill Bergson Lives Dangerously," and "Allrakäraste syster." Her IMDb ID is 0511807, further highlighting her influence in both literature and film.

Augustus, who began his active years in -027, was a prominent figure with a notable family lineage. He was the child of Julius Caesar, Gaius Octavius, and Atia. Augustus had several children, including Tiberius, Gaius Caesar, and Julia the Elder. In his personal life, he was married to Claudia, Livia, and Scribonia. Augustus's military career was marked by his role as commander in several significant battles, including the Battle of Actium, the Battle of Forum Gallorum, and the Battle of Mutina. His leadership was succeeded by Tiberius, while his predecessors included Gnaeus Calpurnius Piso and Caesarion. This structured data highlights Augustus's extensive influence and legacy.

Ayaan Hirsi Ali was born on November 13, 1969, in Mogadishu, Somalia, under the name Ayaan Hirsi Magan. She is known for her critical perspectives on Islam, Islamism, and religion. Hirsi Ali has held positions at prestigious institutions such as the Hoover Institution, Stanford University, and Harvard University. She earned her education at Leiden University in the Netherlands. Barnes Wallis, born Barnes Neville Wallis on September 26, 1887, in Ripley, Derbyshire, was a prominent figure known for his contributions as an inventor and engineer. He passed away on October 30, 1979, in Leatherhead. Wallis's work was marked by innovation, particularly in the development of the bouncing bomb, the earthquake bomb, and the geodesic airframe. His designs also extended to aircraft, including the No. 9r and the Vickers Wild Goose. Recognized for his achievements, he was awarded the Royal Medal and the Albert Medal by the Royal Society of Arts. Additionally, Alfred Egerton Cooper authored a notable work about him, further cementing his legacy in the fields of engineering and invention.
Benedict of Nursia was born on March 2, 480, in Norcia, and he passed away on March 21, 547, in Monte Cassino. He is recognized as the patron saint by several institutions, including Saint Alphonsus Catholic School and St. Elizabeth High School in Delaware. Benito Amilcare Andrea Mussolini was born on July 29, 1883, in Predappio, Italy, to Alessandro Mussolini and Rosa Maltoni. He pursued a career in journalism and later became a prominent political figure. Mussolini was married to both Ida Dalser and Rachele Mussolini, with whom he had children including Romano, Bruno, and Edda. Mussolini's political career was marked by his involvement with several parties, such as the Republican Fascist Party, Fasces of Revolutionary Action, and Italian Fasces of Combat. He served as president during the tenures of Francesco Pricolo and Rodolfo Graziani. As a military commander, he played roles in the Corfu incident, the Mediterranean and Middle East theatre of World War II, and the Greco-Italian War. He led the National Republican Army and Navy. In media, Mussolini founded and published several newspapers, including Il Popolo d'Italia, Il Tevere, and Gerarchia. His influence extended to individuals like Maurice Bardèche, and he was notably known through Domenico Leccisi. Mussolini also led the Fasci Italiani di Combattimento and had various predecessors and successors in his political roles, including Dino Grandi and Luigi Facta. Beyond politics, Mussolini appeared in the film "Ways to Strength and Beauty" and contributed as a writer to "Villafranca." His life ended on April 28, 1945, in the Kingdom of Italy, leaving behind a complex legacy in Italian history.

Bronisław Kasper Malinowski, born on April 7, 1884, in Austria-Hungary, was a prominent figure in the field of social anthropology. He passed away on May 16, 1942, in New Haven, Connecticut. Malinowski held citizenships of both the Austro-Hungarian Empire and Poland. His academic journey began at the Jagiellonian University and later at the London School of Economics, where he laid the foundation for his future contributions. He was influenced by notable scholars such as Charles Gabriel Seligman, James Frazer, and Edvard Westermarck, which shaped his approach to the field. Malinowski is renowned for his work in social anthropology, ethnography, and psychological functionalism. Among his notable works are "Argonauts of the Western Pacific," "The Sexual Life of Savages in North-Western Melanesia," and "Coral Gardens and Their Magic." He mentored several distinguished scholars, including Edmund Leach, Francis L.K. Hsu, and Hilda Kuper. In his personal life, Malinowski was married to Valetta Swann. His contributions remain significant in the realm of anthropology, leaving a lasting legacy through his writings and students.

Caravaggio, born Michelangelo Merisi or Amerighi da Caravaggio on September 29, 1571, in the Duchy of Milan, was a prominent figure in the field of painting. He passed away on July 18, 1610, in Porto Ercole. Trained under Simone Peterzano, Caravaggio is renowned for his notable works such as "Amor Vincit Omnia," "The Seven Works of Mercy," and "The Taking of Christ." His influence extended beyond his own time, as Roberto Longhi is known for his studies on Caravaggio. Additionally, Paolo Facchinetti was part of the team Caravaggio during his career, highlighting the collaborative aspects of his work.
Carl Jung was born as Carl Gustav Jung on July 26, 1875, in the Canton of Thurgau, and he passed away on June 6, 1961, in the Canton of Zurich. Jung pursued his academic journey at the University of Basel and the University of Zurich, where he developed expertise in Psychology and Psychiatry under the guidance of his doctoral advisor, Eugen Bleuler. His work was recognized with awards from the Royal Society of Medicine, the University of Allahabad, and the University of Calcutta. Influenced by notable figures such as Carl Gustav Carus, Meister Eckhart, and Friedrich Nietzsche, Jung made significant contributions to his field, introducing concepts like the Complex, Jungian archetypes, and Analytical psychology. He authored several notable works, including *Psychological Types*, *Memories, Dreams, Reflections*, and *Psychology of the Unconscious*. In his personal life, Jung was married to Emma Jung. He also served as a doctoral advisor to Sabina Spielrein, while Eugen Bleuler was his own doctoral advisor during his academic career.

Charlemagne, active from 768 until 814, was a prominent figure whose life and reign are well-documented. Born to parents Bertrada of Laon and Pepin the Short, Charlemagne succeeded his father and later saw his son Louis the Pious take the throne after him. His military prowess was evident in his command of the Saxon Wars, the Battle of Roncevaux Pass, and the Siege of Pavia. Beyond warfare, Charlemagne was a founder, establishing the Gymnasium Theodorianum, and was known to Richbod for his notable influence. His personal life included marriages to Desiderata of the Lombards, Luitgard, and Fastrada, and he fathered Pepin of Italy, Louis the Pious, and Charles the Younger. Notably, Tekla Teresa Łubieńska authored a significant work about him, highlighting his enduring legacy.
Charles Babbage, a prominent figure in the field of political economy, was born on December 26, 1791. He passed away on October 18, 1871, in Marylebone. Babbage's academic journey included his time at Peterhouse, Cambridge, where he honed his intellectual skills. He was influenced by notable figures such as Robert Woodhouse, Gaspard Monge, and John Herschel, which likely shaped his contributions to his field. Babbage is famously known for inventing the Difference Engine, a significant milestone in the history of computing. On a personal note, he had a child named Benjamin Herschel Babbage. His work was not only influential during his lifetime but also left a lasting legacy, as seen through the contributions of Joseph Clement, who undertook a significant project related to Babbage, and Allan G. Bromley, who is recognized for his work on Babbage.
Charles Darwin, born as Charles Robert Darwin on February 12, 1809, in Shrewsbury, England, passed away on April 19, 1882, in Downe. He was a prominent figure in the fields of Geology and Natural History. Darwin's work was recognized with prestigious awards, including the Pour le Mérite, Royal Medal, and Copley Medal. His intellectual journey was influenced by notable figures such as Alexander von Humboldt, Charles Lyell, and John Herschel. Renowned for his groundbreaking publications, Darwin authored *On the Origin of Species*, *The Descent of Man, and Selection in Relation to Sex*, and *The Voyage of the Beagle*. He also contributed *Insectivorous Plants*, *Geological Observations on South America*, and *Geological Observations on the Volcanic Islands*. In his personal life, Darwin was married to Emma Darwin, and they had several children, including Horace and Henrietta. His father, Robert Darwin, was a significant figure in his early life.
Charles Dickens, born as Charles John Huffam Dickens on February 7, 1812, in Portsmouth, England, was a prominent author known for his literary contributions. He passed away on June 9, 1870, in Higham, Kent. Dickens married Catherine Dickens and had several children, including Dora Annie Dickens, Edward Dickens, Francis Dickens, and Walter Landor Dickens. His notable works include "David Copperfield," "Nicholas Nickleby," and "Oliver Twist." Additionally, he authored "American Notes" and "Memoirs of Joseph Grimaldi." Dickens was also the creator of memorable characters such as Wilkins Micawber and Mrs. Bardell from "Pickwick Papers." He founded "The Daily News" in the UK. His works have been adapted into various films and TV serials, including "Bleak House" (2005 TV serial), "Little Dorrit" (1924 film), and "David Copperfield" (1913 film). Dickens' legacy is further marked by his children, Edward Dickens and Walter Landor Dickens, who are notable as his offspring.
Charles Maurice de Talleyrand-Périgord was born in Paris on February 2, 1754, and died in the same city on May 17, 1838. He pursued his education at the University of Paris and the Church of Saint-Sulpice in Paris. Talleyrand-Périgord had a distinguished career, serving as a politician, diplomat, and clergyman. His political affiliations were diverse, as he identified as a Legitimist, a Doctrinaire, and an Independent politician. In his professional journey, he was both preceded and succeeded by notable figures. Charles-Frédéric Reinhard and Pierre Louis Jean Casimir de Blacas had Talleyrand-Périgord as their predecessor, while Joseph Fouché and Anne-Adrien-Pierre de Montmorency-Laval were succeeded by him. This intricate web of professional relationships highlights his significant role and influence during his tenure.

He passed away on December 25, 1977, in Corsier-sur-Vevey. Chaplin's personal life included marriages to Mildred Harris, Lita Grey, and Paulette Goddard, with whom he had children: Josephine, Victoria, and Christopher. His parents were Hannah Chaplin and Charles Chaplin Sr. Chaplin's artistic contributions were vast. He also composed music for these films. Beyond cinema, Chaplin developed the Montecito Inn and owned Manoir de Ban. Clifford Geertz was born on August 23, 1926. He was married to Hildred Geertz. As a prominent anthropologist, Clifford Geertz served as the doctoral advisor to several notable scholars, including Paul Rabinow and Lawrence Rosen. His work had a broad influence, extending to figures such as Aleksandar Bošković, who was influenced by his ideas. Constantine I, a significant figure in history, held the position of patron saint for the Greek School in Taganrog. He was also recognized as a saint in San Costantino Albanese. Constantine I demonstrated his leadership skills as the builder of the Walls of Constantinople and as the commander during the German and Sarmatian campaigns. In his personal life, he was the child of Helena and the parent of Constans and Crispus. Constantine I was also the spouse of Fausta. His predecessors included Constantius Chlorus, while his successors were Constans, Constantine II, Calocaerus, Maxentius, and Licinius.

Henry Ford, born on July 30, 1863, in Springwells Township, Michigan, was a prominent figure whose life spanned until his death on April 7, 1947, in Dearborn, Michigan. Active from 1891 to 1945, Ford was a man of diverse roles: an engineer, a business magnate, and a philanthropist. He was married to Clara Jane Bryant, and they had a son, Edsel Ford. Politically, Ford was associated with both the Democratic and Republican parties. Ford's most notable contribution was as the founder of the Ford Motor Company, a testament to his innovative spirit. His engineering prowess led to the design of several notable models, including the Ford Model AA, Model B (1904), and Model C. Beyond these, he also played a key role in the establishment of international branches such as Ford Australia, Ford Brasil, and Ford Italia. His influence extended beyond the automotive industry; he was a key figure in organizations like SAE International and the Edison Illuminating Company. Additionally, Ford contributed to the development of the Aerocar (1905 automobile) and manufactured the Ford Quadricycle. He also owned the USS Truant (PYc-14). Following his tenure, John S. Gray succeeded him, marking the continuation of his legacy.
Henry II of England reigned from 1154 until 1189. He was the son of Empress Matilda and Geoffrey V, Count of Anjou, and succeeded Stephen, King of England. Henry II married Eleanor of Aquitaine, and they had several children, including Richard I of England and Eleanor of England, Queen of Castile. He also had a son named Morgan, who became a bishop. Henry II was known for his military leadership, commanding forces in the Battle of Crogen, the Revolt of 1173–1174, and The Anarchy. He was succeeded by his son Richard I of England. Additionally, Henry II was the predecessor to William IX, Count of Poitiers, who later succeeded him. Henry II also had another spouse, Rosamund Clifford. During his reign, he oversaw the construction of several castles, including Hertford Castle, The Castle in Newcastle, and Dover Castle.
Henry VIII of England was a prolific builder, responsible for the construction of Device Forts and Hertford Castle. He also played a significant military role, commanding forces during the Rough Wooing, the Battle of the Spurs, and Bigod's rebellion. In the realm of education, Henry VIII founded several institutions, including Christ Church Cathedral School, Christ College in Brecon, The King's (The Cathedral) School, and Cambridge University Press. Elizabeth Wyckes and Mark Smeaton were among those who served him. Henry VIII was the parent of several children, notably Edward VI, Henry, Duke of Cornwall, and Henry FitzRoy, Duke of Richmond and Somerset. His spouses included Anne of Cleves and Jane Seymour.
Henry V of England was the child of Mary de Bohun and Henry IV of England. He was married to Catherine of Valois, with whom he had a son, Henry VI of England. Henry V succeeded his father, Henry IV, and was later succeeded by his son, Henry VI. He commanded English forces in several significant battles, including the Battle of Agincourt, the Battle of Shrewsbury, and the Hundred Years' War. His active years were recorded from 1413 to 1413, indicating a notable but brief period of prominence.
Hernán Cortés, a prominent figure in history, was born in the Crown of Castile and later passed away in Castilleja de la Cuesta on December 2, 1547. His full name at birth was Hernando Cortés de Monroy y Pizarro Altamirano. Cortés was a Conquistador by occupation and is notable for commanding several significant battles, including the Battle of Cempoala, the Battle of Colhuacatonco, and the Battle of Otumba. His military endeavors were complemented by his role as a founder, as he established both Veracruz City and Mexico City. In his personal life, Cortés had three children: Don, Leonor Cortés Moctezuma, and Martín Cortés, the latter being the son of Malinche. Leonor's parentage is specifically noted as being under Hernán Cortés. Beyond his personal and military achievements, Cortés held significant political roles, with several predecessors and successors in his tenures, including Alonso de Estrada, Alonso de Zuazo, Cristóbal de Tapia, and Rodrigo de Albornoz. These transitions highlight his influence and position within the political structure of his time.
